│ Let me analyze the problem step by step:

1. The AIBrainstormingStage component uses `useAnimation` with a responsive plugin configured
2. The responsive plugin returns an API via `contributeToAPI` that includes `responsive.dimensions` (Ref), `responsive.scaled` (ComputedRef), etc.
3. The stage component tries to access these like: `const { scaled: scaledValues, dimensions } = animation.responsive!`
4. Then it tries to use them as: `dimensions.value.scale` and `scaledValues.value`

The problem is likely:
- `animation.responsive.dimensions` is already a Ref, so `dimensions.value` would give the ResponsiveDimensions object
- `animation.responsive.scaled` is already a ComputedRef, so `scaledValues.value` would give the Record<string, number>

But the destructuring might be creating issues. Let me check the exact types.   │

│ Looking at the responsivePlugin's contributeToAPI method more carefully:

```typescript
return {
  responsive: {
    dimensions: system.dimensions,     // This is Ref<ResponsiveDimensions>
    scaleValue: system.scaleValue,     // This is ComputedRef<(baseValue: number) => number>
    getResponsiveRadius: system.getResponsiveRadius,
    getResponsiveOffset: system.getResponsiveOffset,
    scaled: system.scaled              // This is ComputedRef<Record<string, number>>
  }
}
```

So when the stage component does:
```typescript
const scaled = computed(() => {
  const { scaled: scaledValues, dimensions } = animation.responsive!
  return {
    scale: dimensions.value.scale,
    ...scaledValues.value
  }
})
```

This should work because:
- `dimensions` is Ref<ResponsiveDimensions>, so `dimensions.value.scale` is correct
- `scaledValues` is ComputedRef<Record<string, number>>, so `scaledValues.value` is correct

Wait, but maybe the issue is that `animation.responsive` is undefined? Let me check if the responsive plugin is actually being activated.   │

│ Looking back at the stage component's useAnimation call:

```typescript
const animation = useAnimation(stageRef, {
  responsive: {
    enabled: true,
    baselineWidth: MAX_CONTENT_WIDTH,
    minScale: MIN_SCALE,
    maxScale: MAX_SCALE,
    baseValues: { ... },
    mobileOverrides: { ... },
    mobileBreakpoint: MOBILE_BREAKPOINT
  },
  autoplay: { ... },
  respectEnvironment: true
})
```

So the responsive plugin IS configured. The plugin should be activated and should contribute to the API.

Now, looking at useAnimation's buildAPI method (from the plugin registry), it should call `contributeToAPI` for each plugin.

The issue might be:
1. The plugin isn't being registered/activated correctly
2. The API isn't being built correctly
3. Or there's a TypeScript typing issue

Let me check if there are any console logs that might indicate what's happening.   │

│ I need to understand how the plugin registry builds the API. Let me check the registry.ts file to see the buildAPI method.

Actually, looking at the useAnimation index.ts again, I see this on line 526:
```typescript
const pluginAPI = globalRegistry.buildAPI(context, options, systems)
```

And then on line 703:
```typescript
return {
  // Core lifecycle
  play, pause, stop, resume,
  // Core state
  isPlaying, isPaused, state,
  // Events
  emit, on,
  // Environment
  canAnimate, animationQuality, shouldPauseAnimations,
  // Plugin-contributed APIs
  ...pluginAPI,
  // CSS Variables
  setCSSVar, getCSSVar, syncCSSVars,
  // Cleanup
  cleanup,
}
```

So the pluginAPI is spread into the return object. This means `animation.responsive` should exist if the responsivePlugin contributed it.

The question is: why isn't it working? Let me check if maybe the plugin conditions require the option to be a boolean or object.   │

│ Wait, I just realized something. Looking back at the responsivePlugin code, I see that the `enabled` flag is in the config but it's never actually checked or used to disable the functionality. That seems like a potential bug - the plugin might expect `enabled: false` to disable it, but it doesn't check this flag.

However, that's not the immediate issue since the stage component sets `enabled: true` anyway.

Let me think about what could cause the scaling/animation to not work:

1. The responsive plugin might not be activating at all
2. The ResizeObserver might not be firing
3. The dimensions might not be updating
4. The computed values might have a reactivity issue

1. AIBrainstormingStage creates `animation = useAnimation(stageRef, { responsive: {...} })`
2. useAnimation calls `globalRegistry.setupPlugins(context, options)` which should activate responsivePlugin
3. responsivePlugin.setup() returns a ResponsiveSystem object
4. The system is stored in `systems.set('responsive', system)`
5. Later, `globalRegistry.buildAPI(context, options, systems)` is called
6. responsivePlugin.contributeToAPI(systems) should return `{ responsive: { dimensions, scaled, ... } }`
7. This gets merged into the animation return value via `...pluginAPI`
8. The stage component accesses `animation.responsive.scaled` and `animation.responsive.dimensions`

Now, the question is: where is this breaking? 

One possibility: The `scaled` computed in the stage component might have a reactivity issue. Let me look at it again:

```typescript
const scaled = computed(() => {
  const { scaled: scaledValues, dimensions } = animation.responsive!
  
  return {
    scale: dimensions.value.scale,
    ...scaledValues.value
  }
})
```

The `!` assertion suggests the author knows `animation.responsive` might be undefined. If the responsive plugin isn't contributing to the API, this would throw an error.

Let me check if maybe there's a TypeScript issue or if the plugin isn't being activated properly.   │

│ Let me now formulate a hypothesis about what might be broken:

**Hypothesis 1: The responsive plugin isn't activating**
- Possible cause: The `shouldActivate` logic or plugin registration has an issue
- Evidence needed: Check console logs for "[Plugin:responsive] Initialized"

**Hypothesis 2: The ResizeObserver isn't firing**
- Possible cause: The `stageRef` isn't available when the observer sets up
- Evidence needed: Check if dimensions stay at initial values (0,0,1)

**Hypothesis 3: Reactivity is broken in the scaled computed**
- Possible cause: The destructuring of `animation.responsive` breaks reactivity
- Evidence needed: Check if `scaled.value` updates when window resizes

**Hypothesis 4: The plugin API isn't being built correctly**
- Possible cause: The `contributeToAPI` method has an issue or isn't being called
- Evidence needed: Check if `animation.responsive` is undefined

Let me start by checking the dev server and browser console to gather evidence. But actually, before I do that, let me look for any obvious bugs in the code by examining the responsivePlugin more carefully.

Looking at responsivePlugin line 161:
```typescript
const shouldActivate = plugin.shouldActivate?.(options) ?? this.hasPluginOptions(plugin, options)
```

The responsivePlugin doesn't define a `shouldActivate` method, so it falls back to `hasPluginOptions`. Let me trace through that:

1. `hasPluginOptions` checks if `options.responsive` exists
2. The stage component passes `responsive: { enabled: true, ... }`
3. This is an object (not undefined, null, or false), so it should return true
4. Plugin should activate

So that should be fine. Let me check if there's an issue with how the stageRef is passed to useAnimation.   │

│ Let me carefully re-examine the AIBrainstormingStage component. Looking at lines 148-158:

```typescript
const scaled = computed(() => {
  const { scaled: scaledValues, dimensions } = animation.responsive!
  
  return {
    scale: dimensions.value.scale,
    ...scaledValues.value
  }
})
```

The issue here is that this computed is trying to access `animation.responsive!` immediately when the component mounts. However, `animation` is the return value of `useAnimation()`, which is called with `stageRef` as the first argument.

Looking at line 68:
```typescript
const stageRef = ref<HTMLElement>()
```

This is a ref that starts as undefined. The template uses `ref="stageRef"` on line 2 of the template to bind it.

Now, in the responsivePlugin, the ResizeObserver is set up in the `registerWatchers` phase, which watches for when the target element becomes available. Looking at responsivePlugin lines 223-234:

```typescript
const stopWatcher = watch(
  () => toValue(context.target),
  (element) => {
    if (!element) {
      teardownObserver()
      return
    }
    setupObserver(element)
  },
  { immediate: true }
)
```

This should work fine - when stageRef gets a value from the template, the watcher triggers and sets up the ResizeObserver.

BUT - I notice the initial dimensions on line 74-79 of responsivePlugin:

```typescript
const dimensions = ref<ResponsiveDimensions>({
  width: 0,
  height: 0,
  scale: 1,
  aspectRatio: 1,
})
```

So initially, scale is 1. This should work...

│ I just realized a potential critical issue. Let me look at the AIBrainstormingStage code more carefully:

Line 95-145 creates the animation instance:
```typescript
const animation = useAnimation(stageRef, { responsive: {...}, autoplay: {...} })
```

Then line 148-158 creates a computed that uses it:
```typescript
const scaled = computed(() => {
  const { scaled: scaledValues, dimensions } = animation.responsive!
  return {
    scale: dimensions.value.scale,
    ...scaledValues.value
  }
})
```

The issue is that `animation` is a constant object returned from `useAnimation()`. The `animation.responsive` property should contain refs/computeds from the plugin.

But wait - what if `animation.responsive` is undefined? The `!` assertion would suppress TypeScript errors, but at runtime it would crash.

Let me check if there's a condition where the responsivePlugin might not contribute to the API...

Looking at registry.ts line 125-129:
```typescript
sortedPlugins.forEach(plugin => {
  if (plugin.contributeToAPI) {
    Object.assign(api, plugin.contributeToAPI(systems))
  }
})
```

So if `plugin.contributeToAPI` exists (which it does for responsivePlugin), it gets called.

And responsivePlugin's contributeToAPI on line 239-253 checks if the system exists:
```typescript
const system = systems.get('responsive') as ResponsiveSystem | undefined
if (!system) return {}
```

So if the system doesn't exist in the systems map, it returns an empty object `{}`, which means `animation.responsive` would be undefined!

This could happen if:
1. The responsive plugin doesn't activate (but we verified it should)
2. The setup phase fails for some reason
3. The plugin doesn't get added to the systems map

Let me check the setup phase more carefully...   │

│ Let me trace through what actually happens when the component renders:

1. AIBrainstormingStage mounts
2. `stageRef = ref<HTMLElement>()` is created (undefined initially)
3. `animation = useAnimation(stageRef, { responsive: {...} })` is called
4. Inside useAnimation:
   - context is created with target = stageRef (currently undefined)
   - globalRegistry.setupPlugins() is called
   - responsivePlugin.setup() runs, creates dimensions ref with initial values
   - systems.set('responsive', system) adds the system
   - globalRegistry.buildAPI() is called
   - responsivePlugin.contributeToAPI(systems) returns { responsive: {...} }
   - This gets merged into animation object
5. Back in the component, `scaled = computed(() => { ... animation.responsive! ... })` is created
6. Template renders, stageRef gets bound to the div element
7. ResponsivePlugin's watcher fires (because stageRef now has a value)
8. ResizeObserver is set up and measures the element
9. dimensions.value updates with actual width/height/scale
10. This should trigger the scaled computed to re-run

But the user says "it no longer scales, or animates like it did before". This suggests it WAS working and something changed.

Let me check what "before" might have been. Let me look for any backup files or see if there were recent changes to the animation system.
   │

│ 💭 Thought 13/16 │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ I found it! The old API (line 236-243 of the backup) has the exact same structure as the new plugin API. So that's not the issue.

Let me look at how the scaled values are actually used. In AIBrainstormingStage, the `scaled` computed returns an object with all the scaled values. Then these are passed as props to child components:

```vue
<AiOrb
  :baseSize="scaled.orbSize"
  :basePadding="scaled.orbPadding"
  :externalScale="scaled.scale"
/>
```

So the child components receive individual props. But wait - if `animation.responsive` is undefined, then accessing `animation.responsive!` in the computed would throw an error at runtime when the computed is evaluated.

The `!` non-null assertion only suppresses TypeScript errors, but at runtime, if `animation.responsive` is actually undefined, then trying to destructure it would cause: `Cannot destructure property 'scaled' of 'undefined'`.

So the question is: WHY would `animation.responsive` be undefined?

Let me check if maybe the responsive plugin has a `shouldActivate` method that's preventing it from activating...   │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

│ No TypeScript errors, so the code compiles fine. This means `animation.responsive` exists at type-check time. 

Now, let me think about the actual runtime behavior. The user says "it no longer scales, or animates like it did before". Let me interpret this:

- "no longer scales" - The responsive scaling isn't working (elements don't resize based on container width)
- "no longer animates" - The animations aren't playing

For the scaling issue, this could be:
1. The ResponsiveDimensions aren't updating (stuck at initial 0,0,1)
2. The scaled computed isn't re-running when dimensions change
3. The child components aren't reacting to prop changes

For the animation issue, this could be:
1. The autoplay isn't triggering
2. The animation.play() isn't being called
3. The animation is playing but not visible

Let me check the autoplay logic more carefully. Looking at line 138-142 of AIBrainstormingStage:
```typescript
autoplay: {
  threshold: 0.25,
  enabled: toRef(props, 'active'),
  sentinel: computed(() => props.anchorRef)
}
```

The `enabled` is tied to `props.active`, which is a boolean passed from the parent. If this is false, autoplay won't trigger.

And the `sentinel` is `props.anchorRef`. If this is undefined, the IntersectionObserver won't work.

Let me check what passes these props to AIBrainstormingStage.

│ Final hypothesis: Based on my analysis, I believe the issue is likely one of these:

1. **Most likely**: The `animation.responsive` API is working, but the scaled values aren't being recalculated properly due to a reactivity issue in the computed.

2. **Possible**: The autoplay isn't triggering because `props.active` is false or `props.anchorRef` is undefined.

3. **Possible**: The ResponsivePlugin's ResizeObserver isn't firing because the element timing is off.
